<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification</b> is the qualification process organized by the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">Asian Football Confederation</a> (AFC) to determine the participating teams for the <a href="/wiki/2019_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2019 AFC Asian Cup">2019 AFC Asian Cup</a>, the 17th edition of the international men's <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> championship of Asia. For the first time, the Asian Cup final tournament will be contested by 24 teams, having been expanded from the 16-team format that had been used since <a href="/wiki/2004_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2004 AFC Asian Cup">2004</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ExCO_approval_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-ExCO_approval-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The qualification process will involve four rounds, where the first two doubled as the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(AFC)" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (AFC)">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> for Asian teams.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The proposal to merge the preliminary qualification rounds for FIFA World Cup qualifiers with those for the Asian Cup was ratified by the AFC Competitions Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ExCO_approval_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-ExCO_approval-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The qualification structure is as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ExCO_approval_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-ExCO_approval-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations2019_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-regulations2019-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>First round</b>: A total of 12 teams (teams ranked 35–46) played home-and-away over <a href="/wiki/Two-legged_tie" title="Two-legged tie">two legs</a>. The six winners advanced to the second round.</li>
<li><b>Second round</b>: A total of 40 teams (teams ranked 1–34 and six first round winners) were divided into eight groups of five teams to play home-and-away <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">round-robin</a> matches.
<ul>
<li>The eight group winners and the four best group runners-up advanced to the third round of FIFA World Cup qualification as well as qualify for the AFC Asian Cup finals.</li>
<li>The next 16 highest ranked teams (the remaining four group runners-up, the eight third-placed teams and the four best group fourth-placed teams) advanced directly to the third round of Asian Cup qualification.</li>
<li>The remaining 12 teams entered the play-off round to contest the remaining eight spots in the third round of Asian Cup qualification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa20150413_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-fifa20150413-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>Play-off round</b>: At a Competition Committee meeting in November 2014, it was decided that a play-off round of qualifying would be introduced into the qualification procedure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-play-off_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-play-off-4">[4]</a></sup> There were two rounds of home-and-away two-legged play-off matches to determine the final eight qualifiers for the third round.</li>
<li><b>Third round</b>: The 24 teams were divided into six groups of four to play home-and-away <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">round-robin</a> matches, and they compete for the remaining slots of the 2019 AFC Asian Cup.</li>
</ul>
<p>The play-off round represented a change from the initially announced qualification format – which saw the remaining fourth-placed teams and the four best group fifth-placed teams also advance to the third round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ExCO_approval_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-ExCO_approval-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Entrants">Entrants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Entrants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>46 FIFA-affiliated nations from the AFC entered qualification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In order to determine which nations would compete in the first round and which nations would receive a bye through to the second round, the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a> of January 2015 were used (shown in parentheses).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th style="width:66%">Bye to second round<br/>
(Ranked 1st to 34th)</th>
<th style="width:34%">Competing in first round<br/>
(Ranked 35th to 46th)</th>
</tr>
<tr valign="top">
<td>

<p>Due to the joint format of the FIFA World Cup qualifiers and AFC Asian Cup qualifiers, the hosts of the 2019 AFC Asian Cup, the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_football_team" title="United Arab Emirates national football team">United Arab Emirates</a> also entered the second round of AFC Asian Cup qualifiers despite having qualified automatically.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First_round">First round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_AFC_First_Round" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC First Round">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC First Round</a></div>
<p>The draw for the first round was held on 10 February 2015, 15:30 <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Malaysia" title="Time in Malaysia">MST</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B08:00" title="UTC+08:00">UTC+8</a>), at the AFC House in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preliminary_draw_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-preliminary_draw-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The six teams eliminated from this stage progressed to the <a href="/wiki/2016_AFC_Solidarity_Cup" title="2016 AFC Solidarity Cup">2016 AFC Solidarity Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COMMITTEE_DECISIONS_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-COMMITTEE_DECISIONS-12">[12]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_round">Second round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Second round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_AFC_Second_Round" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC Second Round">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC Second Round</a></div>
<p>The draw for the second round was held on 14 April 2015, 17:00 <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Malaysia" title="Time in Malaysia">MST</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B08:00" title="UTC+08:00">UTC+8</a>), at the JW Marriott Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Groups">Groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed">
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification#Tiebreakers" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification tiebreakers</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>In league format, the ranking of teams in each group is based on the following criteria (regulations Articles 20.6 and 20.7):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-15">[15]</a></sup>
<ol>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Points_(association_football)" title="Points (association football)">Points</a> (3 points for a win, 1 point for a draw, 0 points for a loss)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">Goal difference</a></li>
<li>Goals scored</li>
<li>Points in matches between tied teams</li>
<li>Goal difference in matches between tied teams</li>
<li>Goals scored in matches between tied teams</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Away_goals_rule" title="Away goals rule">Away goals</a> scored in matches between tied teams (if the tie is only between two teams in home-and-away league format)</li>
<li>Fair play points
<ul>
<li>first yellow card: minus 1 point</li>
<li>indirect red card (second yellow card): minus 3 points</li>
<li>direct red card: minus 4 points</li>
<li>yellow card and direct red card: minus 5 points</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Drawing of lots by the FIFA Organising Committee</li>
</ol>
</td>
</tr>
</table>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Malaysia v Saudi Arabia match, on 8 September 2015, was abandoned during the 87th minute after a group of supporters threw objects onto the pitch. At the time of the abandonment the score was 2–1 to Saudi Arabia. On 5 October 2015, FIFA decided that this match was forfeited by Malaysia and the result to be declared as a 3–0 win awarded for Saudi Arabia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>

<td style="white-space:nowrap;font-weight: normal;background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_AFC_Second_Round#Laos_v_Myanmar" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC Second Round">2–2</a></td>
<td style="font-weight: normal;background-color:transparent;">—</td>
</tr>
</table>

Notes:</div>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-table_note_KUW0.03003929603381-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-table_note_KUW0.03003929603381_28-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-table_note_KUW0.03003929603381_28-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-table_note_KUW0.03003929603381_28-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-table_note_KUW0.03003929603381_28-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">On 16 October 2015, FIFA announced that the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Football_Association" title="Kuwait Football Association">Kuwait Football Association</a> (KFA) was suspended with immediate effect, following a decision from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_Executive_Committee" title="FIFA Executive Committee">FIFA Executive Committee</a> that sports law of Kuwait had to be changed before 15 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> The Myanmar v Kuwait match, scheduled for 17 November 2015, was not played due to that suspension,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> and on 13 January 2016, FIFA decided that that match should be forfeited by Kuwait, and awarded as a 3–0 win for Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> The Kuwait v Laos and South Korea v Kuwait matches, scheduled for 24 and 29 March 2016 respectively, did not take place as scheduled, and on 6 April, FIFA decided that those matches should be forfeited by Kuwait, and awarded as 3–0 wins for Laos and South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">FIFA awarded North Korea a 3–0 win as a result of Yemen fielding the ineligible player <a href="/wiki/Mudir_Al-Radaei" title="Mudir Al-Radaei">Mudir Al-Radaei</a>, after North Korea had defeated Yemen 1–0. Al-Radaei failed to serve an automatic one match suspension for receiving two yellow cards earlier in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_AFC_First_Round" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC First Round">First Round</a> of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yemen_sanctioned_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-yemen_sanctioned-29">[25]</a></sup></span></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranking_of_runner-up_teams">Ranking of runner-up teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ranking of runner-up teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To determine the four best runner-up teams, the following criteria are used:</p>
<ol>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Points_(association_football)" title="Points (association football)">Points</a> (3 points for a win, 1 point for a draw, 0 points for a loss)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">Goal difference</a></li>
<li>Goals scored</li>
<li>Play-off match(es) on neutral ground (if approved by FIFA Organizing Committee), with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time_(association_football)" title="Extra time (association football)">extra time</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> if necessary</li>
</ol>
<p>As a result of Indonesia being disqualified due to FIFA suspension, Group F contains only four teams compared to five teams in all other groups. Therefore, the results against the fifth-placed team are not counted when determining the ranking of the runner-up teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ranking_criteria_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-ranking_criteria-31">[26]</a></sup></p>

Rules for classification: 1) Points from matches against teams ranked first, third and fourth in the group; 2) Goal difference from these matches; 3) Goals scored in these matches; 4) Play-off</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranking_of_fourth-placed_teams">Ranking of fourth-placed teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ranking of fourth-placed teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To determine the four best fourth-placed teams, the following criteria were used:</p>
<ol>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Points_(association_football)" title="Points (association football)">Points</a> (3 points for a win, 1 point for a draw, 0 points for a loss)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">Goal difference</a></li>
<li>Goals scored</li>
<li>Play-off match(es) on neutral ground (if approved by AFC Organizing Committee), with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time_(association_football)" title="Extra time (association football)">extra time</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> if necessary</li>
</ol>
<p>As a result of Indonesia being disqualified due to FIFA suspension, Group F contains only four teams compared to five teams in all other groups. Therefore, the results against the fifth-placed team are not counted when determining the ranking of the fourth-placed teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ranking_criteria_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-ranking_criteria-31">[26]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Play-off_round">Play-off round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Play-off round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_Play-off_Round" title="2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification – Play-off Round">2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification – Play-off Round</a></div>
<p>At an AFC Competition Committee meeting in November 2014, it was decided that two rounds of play-off matches would be introduced into the qualification procedure to determine the final eight teams for the main qualifying round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-play-off_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-play-off-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playoff_schedule_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-playoff_schedule-32">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>A total of eight slots for the third round were available from this round (five from round 1, three from round 2).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playoff_schedule_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-playoff_schedule-32">[27]</a></sup> The three teams eliminated from this stage progressed to the <a href="/wiki/2016_AFC_Solidarity_Cup" title="2016 AFC Solidarity Cup">2016 AFC Solidarity Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COMMITTEE_DECISIONS_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-COMMITTEE_DECISIONS-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The draw for the play-off round was held on 7 April 2016, 15:00 <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Malaysia" title="Time in Malaysia">MYT</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B08:00" title="UTC+08:00">UTC+8</a>), at the AFC House in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Round_1">Round 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Round 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Except the lowest seeded team (Bhutan), the other ten teams were drawn into five pairs. Each pair played two matches on 2 and 7 June 2016 with the winners qualifying for the third round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-play-off_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-play-off-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Round_2">Round 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Round 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The five losers from round 1 joined Bhutan in this round. The six teams were drawn into three pairs. Each pair played two matches, with the winners qualifying for the third round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playoff_schedule_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-playoff_schedule-32">[27]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_round">Third round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Third round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_Third_Round" title="2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification – Third Round">2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification – Third Round</a></div>
<p>A total of 24 teams will compete in the third round of AFC Asian Cup qualifiers. Since the 2019 hosts <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_football_team" title="United Arab Emirates national football team">United Arab Emirates</a> have advanced to the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_AFC_Third_Round" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC Third Round">third round of the 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifiers</a>, the automatic slot for the hosts is no longer necessary, and a total of 12 slots for the AFC Asian Cup will be available from this round.</p>
<p>Due to the withdrawal of <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_football_team" title="Guam national football team">Guam</a> and the suspension of <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team" title="Kuwait national football team">Kuwait</a>, the AFC decided to invite both <a href="/wiki/Nepal_national_football_team" title="Nepal national football team">Nepal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau_national_football_team" title="Macau national football team">Macau</a>, the top two teams of the <a href="/wiki/2016_AFC_Solidarity_Cup" title="2016 AFC Solidarity Cup">2016 AFC Solidarity Cup</a>, to re-enter 2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification as replacements in order to maintain 24 teams in the third round of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teamsconfirmed_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-teamsconfirmed-34">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The draw for the third round was held on 23 January 2017, 16:00 <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B04:00" title="UTC+04:00">GST</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teamsconfirmed_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-teamsconfirmed-34">[29]</a></sup> The 24 teams were drawn into six groups of four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Groups_2">Groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed">
<tr>
<th>2019 AFC Asian Cup qualification tiebreakers</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p>The teams are ranked according to <a href="/wiki/Three_points_for_a_win" title="Three points for a win">points</a> (3 points for a win, 1 point for a draw, 0 points for a loss). If tied on points, tiebreakers are applied in the following order (Regulations Article 9.3):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>Points in head-to-head matches among tied teams;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">Goal difference</a> in head-to-head matches among tied teams;</li>
<li>Goals scored in head-to-head matches among tied teams;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Away_goals_rule" title="Away goals rule">Away goals</a> scored in head-to-head matches among tied teams;</li>
<li>If more than two teams are tied, and after applying criteria 1 to 4, a subset of teams are still tied, criteria 1 to 4 are reapplied exclusively to this subset of teams;</li>
<li>Goal difference in all group matches;</li>
<li>Goals scored in all group matches;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">Penalty shoot-out</a> if only two teams are tied and they met in the last round of the group;</li>
<li>Disciplinary points (yellow card = 1 point, red card as a result of two yellow cards = 3 points, direct red card = 3 points, yellow card followed by direct red card = 4 points);</li>
<li>Drawing of lots.</li>
</ol>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
